  <meta content="1. Freshen a Drain (and Shine a Stainless Steel Sink) Instead of using harsh chemicals that could potentially damage your pipes, unclog and refresh your drain by pouring in a  cup of baking soda and 1 cup of vinegar.  Always keep the ratio one-part baking soda to two parts vinegar.  Take the opportunity while surface is damp to sprinkle extra baking soda in the basin of the sink, and give it a good scrub using a scrub brush or dish sponge.  The slightly abrasive qualities of the baking soda should help to remove stuck-on gunk and stains." itemprop="description" name="description"/>

  <meta content="1. Freshen a Drain (and Shine a Stainless Steel Sink) Instead of using harsh chemicals that could potentially damage your pipes, unclog and refresh your drain by pouring in a  cup of baking soda and 1 cup of vinegar.  Always keep the ratio one-part baking soda to two parts vinegar.  Take the opportunity while surface is damp to sprinkle extra baking soda in the basin of the sink, and give it a good scrub using a scrub brush or dish sponge.  The slightly abrasive qualities of the baking soda should help to remove stuck-on gunk and stains." property="og:description"/>
  <meta content="1. Freshen a Drain (and Shine a Stainless Steel Sink) Instead of using harsh chemicals that could potentially damage your pipes, unclog and refresh your drain by pouring in a  cup of baking soda and 1 cup of vinegar.  Always keep the ratio one-part baking soda to two parts vinegar.  Take the opportunity while surface is damp to sprinkle extra baking soda in the basin of the sink, and give it a good scrub using a scrub brush or dish sponge.  The slightly abrasive qualities of the baking soda should help to remove stuck-on gunk and stains." property="twitter:description"/>

                  </div>
                 </div>
                </div>
               </div>
              </div>
              <div class="Pos-r D-ib Cur-d Va-t" style="height:40px;">
               <div class="D-ib" style="height:40px;padding:0 11.5px;">

                </div>

                </div>
                <div class="pop-out Op-0" style="position:absolute;overflow:hidden;margin-top:-3px;margin-left:0px;top:40px;left:auto;right:-11.5px;display:inline-block;transition-property:opacity;transition-duration:0.1s;transition-timing-function:linear;pointer-events:none;">
                 <div style="position:relative;background-color:white;-webkit-border-radius:5px;-moz-border-radius:5px;-khtml-border-radius:5px;border-radius:5px;border:solid 1px #e7e7e7;padding:4px;z-index:2147483645;">

          <div class="Pos-r Z-0 article-container" data-template="desktop" id="article-115953009700" style="background-color:white;min-height:315px;">
           <div class="Pos-r sticky-container print-article" style="min-height:315px;">
            <div class="article-inner-container" style="max-width:1280px;">
             <div class="inset-container Mx-a">
              <div class="GridTable">
               <div class="D-tbr row-template">
                <div class="GridTable-Cell Va-t col-left">
                 <div class="content" style="width:825px;min-width:825px;">
                  <noscript>
                  </noscript>
                  <noscript>
                  </noscript>
                  <div class="GridTable grid-content">
                   <div class="D-tbr row-content">
                    <div class="GridTable-Cell Va-t col-left Pend-20" style="width:305px;max-width:305px;">
                     <h1 class="Font-A-6-110 title W-100" id="article-aft-title-115953009700">
                      The 2-Ingredient Powerhouse That Cleans Almost Anything
                     </h1>
                     <div class="attribution-component D-b W-100" id="article-aft-attribution-115953009700" style="max-width:305px;">
                      <div class="author-info author-info-text-first Pt-10 W-100 Bd-t Bd-b Bdstart-0 Bdend-0">
                       <div class="GridTable W-100">
                        <div class="D-tbr">
                         <div class="GridTable-Cell Va-t">
                          <cite class="byline col D-b Fs-n" style="padding-bottom:15px;">
                           <span class="author-name Font-C-2-140 D-b">
                            <a class="attribution-name Font-C-2-140 Fw-b Whs-n" data-ylk="t1:a2;t2:article;t3:cat;t8:0d63089c-a54f-3d82-bce7-9ecfcfc5ec43;t9:17;elm:itm;elmt:link;itc:0" href="http://www.bobvila.com/" style="color:#000;" target="_blank">
                             Bob Vila
                            </a>
                           </span>
                           <time class="date Font-C-2-140 Fw-n D-b">
                            <span>
                             May 2, 2015
                            </span>
                           </time>
                          </cite>
                         </div>
                        </div>
                       </div>
                      </div>
                     </div>
                    </div>
                    <div class="GridTable-Cell Va-t col-right" style="max-width:500px;">
                     <div class="text-body-wrapper W-100 Font-B-1-160">
                      <noscript>
                      </noscript>
                      <div class="text-body W-100 Font-B-1-160" id="article-aft-text-body-115953009700" style="color:#222222;max-width:500px;">
                       <div class="body read-more-cut">
                        <div class="pre-cut" style="height:auto;margin-bottom:1.5em;">
                         <p>
                          <i>
                           Caylin Harris
                          </i>
                          <br/>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          Its almost hard to believe: By combining two seemingly mild pantry staples, you can handle most of the tougher messes in your home. But the fact is that, most of the time, baking soda and vinegar are the only one-two punch you need to get your home clean. Seriously! The secret is in how you apply the two, as too much of either can neutralize both. So long as you remember these recipes, though, you can always be ready to clean everyday messes and your homes grimiest corners.
                         </p>
                         <figure>
                          <img alt="The 2-Ingredient Powerhouse That Cleans Almost Anything" height="393" src="https://s.yimg.com/cd/resizer/2.0/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w540/09a5713b61a98dc0eec4cc5e0f89db6594a485e3.jpg" width="540"/>
                         </figure>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           1. Freshen a Drain (and Shine a Stainless Steel Sink)
                          </b>
                          <br/>
                          Instead of using harsh chemicals that could potentially damage your pipes,
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:0d63089c-a54f-3d82-bce7-9ecfcfc5ec43;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://www.bobvila.com/articles/267-quick-tip-fixing-a-clogged-drain/" target="_blank">
                           unclog and refresh your drain
                          </a>
                          by pouring in a  cup of baking soda and 1 cup of vinegar. Always keep the ratio one-part baking soda to two parts vinegar. The mixture will fizz and bubble, like your favorite middle school volcano science project. Once it dies down, flush the drain with very hot water for five minutes, then run the cold water.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          Take the opportunity while surface is damp to sprinkle extra baking soda in the basin of the sink, and give it a good scrub using a scrub brush or dish sponge. The slightly abrasive qualities of the baking soda should help to remove stuck-on gunk and stains.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           2. Solve Hard Water Stains
                          </b>
                          <br/>
                          Give tough
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:0d63089c-a54f-3d82-bce7-9ecfcfc5ec43;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://www.bobvila.com/articles/how-to-remove-hard-water-stains/" target="_blank">
                           hard water stains
                          </a>
                          the boot! Place a cloth or paper towel soaked with vinegar over the affected area and let it sit for a few hours. Remove the cloth, scrub with a baking soda paste (a mixture of dry baking soda and just enough water to create a paste-like consistency), spritz lightly with vinegar, and wipe clean.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           RELATED:
                           <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:0d63089c-a54f-3d82-bce7-9ecfcfc5ec43;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://www.bobvila.com/what-not-to-dump-down-sink/47944-7-kitchen-sink-sins-to-avoid/slideshows" target="_blank">
                            7 Kitchen Sink Sins to Avoid
                           </a>
                          </b>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           3. Reverse Carpet Stains
                          </b>
                          <br/>
                          With these cleaners up your sleeveor, rather, sitting in your pantryyou need not cringe when a guest spills a bit of drink
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:0d63089c-a54f-3d82-bce7-9ecfcfc5ec43;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://www.bobvila.com/before-you-start/48246-how-to-get-rid-of-every-carpet-stain/slideshows" target="_blank">
                           on your carpet
                          </a>
                          . Create a paste with baking soda and a small amount of vinegar, then work it into the stained carpet fibers with your fingers. Allow the mixture to sit and dry overnight, then vacuum up any remnants. Before trying out this tip on a large area, test it on small, out-of-sight patch of carpet first. If everything looks kosher, treat the rest of your stain.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           RELATED:
                           <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:0d63089c-a54f-3d82-bce7-9ecfcfc5ec43;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://www.bobvila.com/dinner-napkins/46712-the-morning-after-13-lifesaving-party-cleanup-tips/slideshows" target="_blank">
                            The Morning After - 13 Lifesaving Party Cleanup Tips
                           </a>
                          </b>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           4. Kill Mildew in a Load of Laundry
                          </b>
                          <br/>
                          Baking soda and vinegars cleaning and deodorizing properties
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:0d63089c-a54f-3d82-bce7-9ecfcfc5ec43;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://www.bobvila.com/articles/how-to-get-rid-of-mildew-smell/" target="_blank">
                           work wonders in the wash
                          </a>
                          . Add  cup of baking soda in with your detergent to help boost its cleaning power. One cup of vinegar poured in during the rinse cycle will help kill bacteria in the load and doubles as a chemical-free fabric softener.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           RELATED:
                           <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:0d63089c-a54f-3d82-bce7-9ecfcfc5ec43;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://www.bobvila.com/smelly-towels/48512-9-smart-hacks-for-laundry-day/slideshows" target="_blank">
                            9 Smart Hacks for Laundry Day
                           </a>
                          </b>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           5. Whiten and Brighten Grout
                          </b>
                          <br/>
                          The abrasive qualities of baking soda add muscle to your own scrubbing efforts. Nowhere could use that extra oomph more than
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:0d63089c-a54f-3d82-bce7-9ecfcfc5ec43;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://www.bobvila.com/articles/cleaning-grout/" target="_blank">
                           your stained grout
                          </a>
                          ! Make a paste using baking soda and water, spritz lightly with vinegar, and immediately scrub and rinse the area. Full disclosure: Youll probably still need a little bit of musclejust think of these power players as your line of backup.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           RELATED:
                           <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:0d63089c-a54f-3d82-bce7-9ecfcfc5ec43;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://www.bobvila.com/how-to-remove-soap-scum/48495-8-unusual-tips-for-your-cleanest-bathroom-ever/slideshows" target="_blank">
                            8 Unusual Tips for Your Cleanest Bathroom Ever
                           </a>
                          </b>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           6. Get Rid of Gunk on Pots and Pans
                          </b>
                          <br/>
                          Dried-on food particles, baked-on grime, and burnt dinner remains all can add time on to your dinner cleanupbut theyre no match for this power couple. Sprinkle baking soda on damp (not wet) pots and pans, spritz with vinegar, then go to town scrubbing with a nylon dish sponge. The slight foaming action will break up some of the tougher stuck-on food, leaving you with a little extra energy after
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:0d63089c-a54f-3d82-bce7-9ecfcfc5ec43;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://www.bobvila.com/rinse-dishes-before-dishwasher/48154-your-dishwasher-can-do-better-9-tips-to-boost-performance/slideshows" target="_blank">
                           dish duty
                          </a>
                          .
                         </p>
                        </div>
                        <div class="post-cut W-100" id="post-cut" style="transition-property:none;-webkit-transition-property:none;transition-duration:10s;-webkit-transition-duration:10s;transition-timing-function:ease-in;-webkit-transition-timing-function:ease-in;overflow:hidden;max-height:999999px;max-width:500px;">
                         <figure>
                          <img alt="image" data-src="https://s.yimg.com/cd/resizer/2.0/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w540/9983d469a8a787c635c944394d37c616b2549faf.jpg" height="393" src="https://s.yimg.com/g/images/spaceball.gif" width="540"/>
                         </figure>
                        </div>
                       </div>
                      </div>

root.App.Cache.genUrl = function (routeName, context) {
        var route = routeMap[routeName],
            path, keys, i, len, key, param, regex;

        if (!route) { return ''; }

        path = route.path;
        keys = route.keys;

        if (context &amp;&amp; (len = keys.length)) {
            for (i = 0; i &lt; len; i += 1) {
                key   = keys[i];
                param = key.name || key;
                regex = new RegExp('[:*]' + param + '\\b');
                path  = path.replace(regex, context[param]);
            }
        }

        // Replace missing params with empty strings.
        return path.replace(/([:*])([\w\-]+)?/g, '');
    };

Or use it to make peeling garlic a cinch? It&#x2019;s true!\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F8e077c37312a32ff9c53c4b84cf1e8d577daa0c9.jpg\" alt=\"Peel Garlic in 20 Seconds? 3 Things You Didn&apos;t Know Your Microwave Could Do\" width=\"540\" height=\"360\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EWe&#x2019;ve got three awesome \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.oola.com\u002Fcooking-tips\u002F8873\u002F17-crazy-fast-and-easy-microwave-snack-hacks-muglife#slide\u002F0\"\u003Emicrowave uses\u003C\u002Fa\u003E that are anything but ordinary. Once you discover the power of the microwave, we&#x2019;re pretty sure it&#x2019;ll be your new best friend in the kitchen.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Ci\u003EMake Scrambled Eggs in the Microwave\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EHere&#x2019;s a breakfast game changer for you! Once you realize you can make scrambled egg in a microwave, having breakfast at the office doesn&#x2019;t have to mean a cold bowl of cereal or the last soggy danish left on the tray.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EIngredients\u002FMaterials:\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cul\u003E\n \u003Cli\u003E2 eggs\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n \u003Cli\u003ESplash of milk\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n \u003Cli\u003EMug\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n \u003Cli\u003EFork\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n \u003Cli\u003EMicrowave\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EInstructions:\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E1. Crack two eggs into a microwave safe mug and add milk.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E2. Whisk with a fork to combine.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E3. Microwave on high for 45 seconds and remove.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E4. Scramble gently with fork and return to microwave for a further 30-45 seconds.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E5. Enjoy!\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Ci\u003EMake Parmesan Cheese Bowls in the Microwave\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EImpress your guests by serving appetizers and salads in individual edible parmesan bowls.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EIngredients\u002FMaterials:\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cul\u003E\n \u003Cli\u003EShredded parmesan cheese\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n \u003Cli\u003EParchment paper square\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n \u003Cli\u003ETwo small bowls\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n \u003Cli\u003EMicrowave\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EInstructions:\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E1. &#xA0;Mound a large handful of parmesan on a square of baking parchment, and gently press and spread to create a circle of cheese. &#xA0;You want the diameter of the circle to be slightly larger than the diameter of your bowl.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E2. Place the parchment in the microwave and cook on high for about a minute to a minute and a half. Keep an eye on the cheese - you want to it be golden brown. While it cooks, get your two bowls ready, so that you can work quickly.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E3. Open the microwave door and place one bowl, right side up, in the middle of the cheese round.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E4. Pull the parchment out of the microwave, keeping the bowl on top, and quickly flip it.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E5. Place the other bowl, upside down, on top of the parchment and press down. Your parmesan cheese round and the parchment should be squeezed between the two bowls. Hold for 10-15 seconds until cheese hardens.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E6. Remove bowls and parchment. You will be left with a delicious bowl made of cheese! Now fill it as you please.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated on Yahoo Makers: \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fmakers\u002Fcookie-butter-cake-in-a-mug-that-you-can-make-in-118704109175.html\"\u003EMake the World&#x2019;s Tastiest Mug Cake in Your Microwave\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Ci\u003EPeel Garlic More Quickly\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EPeeling garlic is never the highlight of making a meal. The cloves can be difficult to get out of their skins, and whacking them with blunt force seems so brutal! The microwave can make things so much easier.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EIngredients\u002FMaterials:\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cul\u003E\n \u003Cli\u003EHead of garlic\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n \u003Cli\u003EMicrowave\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EInstructions:\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E1. Place a whole head of garlic in the microwave for 20-30 seconds.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E2. Remove from microwave and with very little effort, the cloves will pop right out of their skins.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ENote: The head of garlic will be quite warm, so if you have sensitive hands, pop on some kitchen gloves.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" alt=\"image\" width=\"540\" height=\"360\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F73a08d490be616cc0b928e7d60382a3bf49f4b3f.jpg\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EAlso on Yahoo Makers:\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Ciframe width=\"640\" height=\"360\" allowfullscreen=\"true\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fscreen.yahoo.com\u002Fhard-boiled-eggs-234611836.html?format=embed\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fiframe\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Ci\u003ELet Yahoo Makers inspire you every day! But the fact is that, most of the time, baking soda and vinegar are the only one-two punch you need to get your home clean. Seriously! The secret is in how you apply the two, as too much of either can neutralize both. So long as you remember these recipes, though, you can always be ready to clean everyday messes and your home&#x2019;s grimiest corners.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F09a5713b61a98dc0eec4cc5e0f89db6594a485e3.jpg\" alt=\"The 2-Ingredient Powerhouse That Cleans Almost Anything\" width=\"540\" height=\"393\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E1. Freshen a Drain (and Shine a Stainless Steel Sink)\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cbr\u003EInstead of using harsh chemicals that could potentially damage your pipes, \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.bobvila.com\u002Farticles\u002F267-quick-tip-fixing-a-clogged-drain\u002F\"\u003Eunclog and refresh your drain\u003C\u002Fa\u003E by pouring in a &#xBD; cup of baking soda and 1 cup of vinegar. Always keep the ratio one-part baking soda to two parts vinegar. The mixture will fizz and bubble, like your favorite middle school volcano science project. Once it dies down, flush the drain with very hot water for five minutes, then run the cold water.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ETake the opportunity while surface is damp to sprinkle extra baking soda in the basin of the sink, and give it a good scrub using a scrub brush or dish sponge. The slightly abrasive qualities of the baking soda should help to remove stuck-on gunk and stains.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E2. Solve Hard Water Stains\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cbr\u003EGive tough \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.bobvila.com\u002Farticles\u002Fhow-to-remove-hard-water-stains\u002F\"\u003Ehard water stains\u003C\u002Fa\u003E the boot! Place a cloth or paper towel soaked with vinegar over the affected area and let it sit for a few hours. Remove the cloth, scrub with a baking soda paste (a mixture of dry baking soda and just enough water to create a paste-like consistency), spritz lightly with vinegar, and wipe clean.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERELATED: \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.bobvila.com\u002Fwhat-not-to-dump-down-sink\u002F47944-7-kitchen-sink-sins-to-avoid\u002Fslideshows\"\u003E7 Kitchen Sink Sins to Avoid\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E3. Reverse Carpet Stains\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cbr\u003EWith these cleaners up your sleeve&#x2014;or, rather, sitting in your pantry&#x2014;you need not cringe when a guest spills a bit of drink \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.bobvila.com\u002Fbefore-you-start\u002F48246-how-to-get-rid-of-every-carpet-stain\u002Fslideshows\"\u003Eon your carpet\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. Create a paste with baking soda and a small amount of vinegar, then work it into the stained carpet fibers with your fingers. Allow the mixture to sit and dry overnight, then vacuum up any remnants. Before trying out this tip on a large area, test it on small, out-of-sight patch of carpet first. If everything looks kosher, treat the rest of your stain.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERELATED: \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.bobvila.com\u002Fdinner-napkins\u002F46712-the-morning-after-13-lifesaving-party-cleanup-tips\u002Fslideshows\"\u003EThe Morning After - 13 Lifesaving Party Cleanup Tips\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E4. Kill Mildew in a Load of Laundry\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cbr\u003EBaking soda and vinegar&#x2019;s cleaning and deodorizing properties \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.bobvila.com\u002Farticles\u002Fhow-to-get-rid-of-mildew-smell\u002F\"\u003Ework wonders in the wash\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. Add &#xBD; cup of baking soda in with your detergent to help boost its cleaning power. One cup of vinegar poured in during the rinse cycle will help kill bacteria in the load and doubles as a chemical-free fabric softener.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERELATED: \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.bobvila.com\u002Fsmelly-towels\u002F48512-9-smart-hacks-for-laundry-day\u002Fslideshows\"\u003E9 Smart Hacks for Laundry Day\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E5. Whiten and Brighten Grout\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cbr\u003EThe abrasive qualities of baking soda add muscle to your own scrubbing efforts. Nowhere could use that extra &#x201C;oomph&#x201D; more than \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.bobvila.com\u002Farticles\u002Fcleaning-grout\u002F\"\u003Eyour stained grout\u003C\u002Fa\u003E! Make a paste using baking soda and water, spritz lightly with vinegar, and immediately scrub and rinse the area. Full disclosure: You&#x2019;ll probably still need a little bit of muscle&#x2014;just think of these power players as your line of backup.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERELATED: \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.bobvila.com\u002Fhow-to-remove-soap-scum\u002F48495-8-unusual-tips-for-your-cleanest-bathroom-ever\u002Fslideshows\"\u003E8 Unusual Tips for Your Cleanest Bathroom Ever\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E6. Get Rid of Gunk on Pots and Pans\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cbr\u003EDried-on food particles, baked-on grime, and burnt dinner remains all can add time on to your dinner cleanup&#x2014;but they&#x2019;re no match for this power couple.
